What Invalidates Sajdah al-Tilawah and the Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Its Completion
Explains invalidators of sajdah al-tilawah and the intra-Hanafi dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the invalidators of sajdah al-tilawah and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the moment of its completion, including the practical consequences.

Core Idea
When sajdah al-tilawah is considered complete determines whether an invalidating act requires repetition—a key dispute between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad.

Sajdah al-tilawah is a wajib act upon reciting or hearing a verse of prostration. Like prayer, certain acts can invalidate it, but the exact point at which it becomes 'complete' affects whether an invalidator requires repetition. Hanafi masters differed on this, with practical implications for the mufti and the layperson.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Invalidators
List the acts that invalidate sajdah al-tilawah according to the passage: speaking, loud laughter (qahqaha), and breaking wudu (hadath) – whether intentional or by mistake.
Loud laughter does not require wudu, as previously established in the chapter on taharah.
2
Understand the Analogy to Prayer
The ruling that these acts require repetition is based on qiyas (analogy) to the prayer (salat), where such acts invalidate the act of worship.
This analogy is the basis for the default position.
3
Recognize the Completion Dispute
Imam Muhammad holds that sajdah is complete only after both placing the forehead and raising it. Abu Yusuf holds that it is complete upon placing the forehead alone.
This is the central ikhtilaf driving different rulings.
4
Analyze Al-Kamal's Evaluation and the Counter-Argument
Al-Kamal ibn al-Humam finds Abu Yusuf's view good (hasan), but the author adds a reflection: even if raising is not integral, one is still in the act of prostration while the forehead is down, so an invalidator at that moment corrupts the part it contacts, voiding the whole.
This suggests the issue requires further reflection (falyatammal).
5
Determine Practical Consequences
If one laughs after placing but before raising: according to Muhammad, repetition is required; according to Abu Yusuf, it is not. The mufta bihi is not definitively given, but Al-Kamal's preference leans toward Abu Yusuf.
This difference is the thamarah al-khilaf.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تنبيه آخر في بيان ما يبطل هذه السجدة وما لا يبطلها: إذا تكلم فيها، أو قهقه، أو أحدث متعمداً، أو خطأ، فعليه إعادتها اعتباراً بالصلوية، ولا وضوء عليه في القهقهة فيها اتفاقاً، لما قدمناه في الطهارة، وإن سبقه الحدث توضأ وأعادها، قال شيخ الإسلام هذا الجواب مستقيم على قول محمد رحمه الله، فإن عنده تمام السجدة بوضع الجبهة ورفعها، فإذا أحدث فيها أو ضحك أو تكلم أعادها، أما على قول أبي يوسف رحمه الله : تمام السجدة بوضع الجبهة لا غير، فإذا وضعت الجبهة فقد تمت السجدة، وإن قل، فكيف يتصور القهقهة أو الكلام ونحوه فيها، وإذا ضحك بعد ذلك فقد ضحك بعد تمام السجدة، فلا يلزمه الإعادة، كذا في ( التاتارخانية)، قال الكمال: وهو حسن، انتهى. وقد يقال: الرفع وإن لم يكن من تمامها فما دام في الوضع فهو فيها، كمن أطال القراءة والقيام وهو في الفرض، فإذا قهقه أو عمل المنافي حصل في حقيقة السجود، مبطل الجزء الملاقي له، فيبطل الكل ببطلانه، فليتأمل.
Another note explaining what invalidates this prostration and what does not: If he speaks during it, or laughs loudly, or breaks his wudu intentionally or by mistake, he must repeat it by analogy with prayer. There is no wudu upon him for loud laughter in it by agreement, due to what we presented in Taharah. If an event (hadath) precedes, he performs wudu and repeats. Shaykh al-Islam said: This answer is correct according to the saying of Muhammad, may Allah have mercy on him, for according to him the completion of the prostration is by placing the forehead and raising it. So if he breaks wudu or laughs or speaks during it, he repeats it. As for the saying of Abu Yusuf, may Allah have mercy on him: The completion of the prostration is by placing the forehead only. So when the forehead is placed, the prostration is completed, even if briefly. How then can one imagine loud laughter or speech or the like during it? If he laughs after that, he has laughed after completion of the prostration, so repetition is not required of him. This is in (al-Tatarkhaniyyah). Al-Kamal said: This is good. It may be said: Although raising is not part of its completion, as long as he is in the state of placing, he is in it, like one who prolongs reading and standing in the obligatory prayer; if he laughs or does something contrary, it occurs in the reality of prostration, invalidating the part it contacts, so the whole is invalidated by its invalidation. So reflect.
Source pages p. 515

Commentary
This passage is a note (tanbih) discussing what invalidates sajdah al-tilawah and what does not. The general rule is that if one speaks, laughs (qahqaha), or breaks wudu intentionally or by mistake during the prostration, one must repeat it, analogizing to prayer. However, it is agreed that loud laughter does not necessitate wudu (as discussed earlier in the chapter on taharah). If an impurity (hadath) occurs, one must perform wudu and repeat. The central dispute revolves around when the prostration is considered complete. According to Imam Muhammad, the prostration is complete only after both placing the forehead and raising it; thus, any invalidating act during that entire period requires repetition. According to Abu Yusuf, placing the forehead alone completes the prostration; therefore, acts after placing do not require repetition. Al-Kamal ibn al-Humam finds Abu Yusuf's view good. The author then offers a critical reflection: even if raising is not integral, as long as one is still in the act of placing, any invalidator nullifies the part it contacts, thus nullifying the whole. This is presented as a point for reflection (falyatammal), indicating a nuanced position.

Key Terms
تمام السجدة (tamam al-sajdah): The moment when the prostration is considered complete; disputed between placing only or placing and raising.
قهقهة (qahqaha): Loud, audible laughter that invalidates prayer and, by analogy, sajdah al-tilawah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Muhammad, when is sajdah al-tilawah considered complete?
A) Upon placing the forehead.
B) Upon both placing and raising the forehead.
C) After saying the takbir.
D) Upon intention.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school contains an internal dispute on the completion of sajdah al-tilawah, with practical consequences for when an invalidator requires repetition.

Recommended Supplications for Sajdah al-Tilawah
Lists recommended supplications during prostration of recitation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the primary recommended supplication for sajdah al-tilawah and identify alternative permissible formulas according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
The most sound view is to recite 'Subhana Rabbi al-A'la' in sajdah al-tilawah, just as in prayer prostration, though multiple authentic supplications are permissible.

In this lesson, we explore what to recite during the prostration of recitation. While Imam Muhammad did not specify a formula, later Hanafi scholars determined that saying the same glorification as in prayer prostration is preferred. However, other options are also valid, depending on context — whether the prostration occurs during prayer (obligatory or voluntary) or outside prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core question
The passage addresses the supplication (tasbih) recited in sajdah al-tilawah. Note that Imam Muhammad did not explicitly prescribe a formula.
2
Recognize the preferred view
The soundest opinion (al-ashah) is to say the same glorification as in the prostration of prayer: 'Subhana Rabbi al-A'la'. This is based on analogy (qiyas) because prayer prostration is superior.
This view is adopted by Abu Bakr al-Iskafi and Abu al-Layth al-Samarqandi.
3
Note alternative opinions
Some scholars recommend other supplications such as 'Rabbi inni zalamtu nafsi faghfir li' or the verse 'Subhana Rabbina in kana wa'du Rabbina la maf'ula'. The hadith from Aisha also reports a longer du'a for night prostrations.
4
Apply contextual differentiation
Al-Kamal ibn al-Humam explains that the choice depends on context: in obligatory prayer, stick to 'Subhana Rabbi al-A'la'; in voluntary prayer, any reported du'a is fine; outside prayer, all transmitted supplications are permissible.
This resolves the apparent conflict between opinions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تنبيه: لم يذكر ما يقال فيها من التسبيح لأنه قال في (المبسوط ) : لم يذكر محمد رحمه الله ماذا يقول في سجدوه، والأصح أن يقول فيه من التسبيح ما يقول في سجود الصلاة، وبه قال الشافعي رحمه الله كذا في (معراج الدراية) انتهى. قال في ( التاتارخانية ) : وفي ( الخانية ) : هو الصحيح، وقال أبو بكر الإسكافي: لأن سجدة الصلاة أفضل من سجدة التلاوة، ويقال فيها: سبحان ربي الأعلى، فكذلك هذا، قال الفقيه أبو الليث : وبه نأخذ، وفي ( الينابيع) : يقول: سبحان ربي الأعلى ثلاثاً، وذلك أدناه، وفي الظهيرية : وهو الأصح انتهى. وفي شرح ( الكنز للديري ) : وقد اختلف مشايخنا في ماذا يقول في سجود التلاوة، فقال بعضهم: يقول ربِّ إني ظلمت نفسي فاغفر لي، انتهى. وكذا في (جامع الجوامع)، وقال بضعهم: يقول: (سُبْحَانَ رَبِّنَا إِن كَانَ وَعْدُ رَبِّنَا لَمَفْعُولًا) [الإسراء: 108]، انتهى. ونقله في ( المحيط) عن بعض المتأخرين، كما في ( التاتارخانية)، وفي ( السنن عن عائشة: كان رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم يقول في سجود القرآن بالليل مراراً إذا سجد: سجد وجهي للذي خلقه وصوره وشق سمعه وبصره بحوله وقوته ) كذا في (شرح الديري)، وقال المحقق الكمال بن الهمام: وينبغي أن لا يكون ما صحح على عمومه، فإن كانت السجدة في الصلاة يقول فيها ما يقال فيها، فإن كانت فريضة قال: سبحان ربي الأعلى، أو نفلاً قال ما شاء مما ورد ك: سجد وجهي للذي خلقه ... إلخ، وقوله: (اللهم اكتب لي عندك بها أجراً، وضع عني بها وزراً، واجعلها لي عندك ذخراً، وتقبلها مني كما تقبلتها من عبدك داود)، وإن كان خارج الصلاة قال كل ما أثر من ذلك، انتهى. والله أعلم.
Note: He did not mention what is said in it of glorification because he said in (al-Mabsut): Muhammad did not mention what one says in his prostration. The most correct is that he says in it of glorification what he says in the prostration of prayer, and al-Shafi'i said likewise. In (Tatarkhaniyyah) and (al-Khaniyyah): It is correct. Abu Bakr al-Iskafi said: Because the prostration of prayer is superior to the prostration of recitation, and one says in it 'Subhana Rabbi al-A'la', so likewise this. Al-Faqih Abu al-Layth said: We take this. In (al-Yanabi'): He says 'Subhana Rabbi al-A'la' three times, and that is the minimum. In (al-Zahiriyyah): It is the most correct. In Sharh al-Kanz by al-Dayri: Our scholars differed on what one says in the prostration of recitation. Some said: He says 'Rabbi inni zalamtu nafsi faghfir li'. In (Jami' al-Jawami), some said: He says 'Subhana Rabbina in kana wa'du Rabbina la maf'ula' [al-Isra: 108]. It is reported in (al-Muhit) from some later scholars. In (al-Sunan) from Aisha: The Messenger of Allah used to say in the prostration of the Quran at night repeatedly when he prostrated: 'Sajada wajhi li alladhi khalaqahu wa sawwarahu wa shaqqa sam'ahu wa basarahu bihawlihi wa quwwatihi.' Al-Muhaqqiq al-Kamal ibn al-Humam said: This should not be taken as absolute. If the prostration is in prayer, he says what is said in it. If it is an obligatory prayer, he says 'Subhana Rabbi al-A'la'; if voluntary, he says whatever is reported like 'Sajada wajhi...' and 'Allahumma uktub li...'. If it is outside prayer, he says all that is transmitted. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 515

Commentary
This note (tanbih) addresses the supplications (tasbih) recited during sajdah al-tilawah. Imam Muhammad did not specify a particular recitation. The soundest view (al-ash) is to say the same glorification as in the prostration of prayer, namely 'Subhana Rabbi al-A'la' (Glory to my Lord, the Most High). This is because the prostration in prayer is superior. This is adopted by Abu Bakr al-Iskafi and Abu al-Layth al-Samarqandi, and it is the relied-upon position for fatwa. Some scholars recommend saying it three times. Others suggest alternative supplications: 'Rabbi inni zalamtu nafsi faghfir li' (My Lord, I have wronged myself, so forgive me), or the Quranic verse 'Subhana Rabbina in kana wa'du Rabbina la maf'ula'. The hadith from Aisha reports that the Prophet used to say a longer supplication during night prostrations. Al-Kamal ibn al-Humam contextualizes these: the specific supplication depends on whether the prostration occurs during prayer (obligatory or voluntary) or outside prayer. The passage thus presents a range of valid options while emphasizing the primacy of the glorification from prayer prostration.

Key Terms
سبحان ربي الأعلى (subhana rabbi al-a'la): The glorification recited in prostration; the recommended phrase for sajdah al-tilawah by analogy with prayer prostration.
سجد وجهي للذي خلقه (sajada wajhi li alladhi khalaqahu): A longer supplication reported from the Prophet for prostration of recitation at night.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the most correct (ashah) supplication to say in sajdah al-tilawah according to the passage?
A) 'Sajada wajhi li alladhi khalaqahu'
B) 'Subhana Rabbi al-A'la'
C) 'Rabbi inni zalamtu nafsi faghfir li'
D) 'Allahumma uktub li biha ajra'

Key Takeaway
The relied-upon Hanafi position is to say 'Subhana Rabbi al-A'la' in sajdah al-tilawah, but other authentic supplications are permitted based on context.

The Ruling on Sajdat al-Shukr (Prostration of Thanks)
Dispute between Abu Hanifa and the two companions on Sajdat al-Shukr.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three Hanafi positions on Sajdat al-Shukr, evaluate the evidence for each, and apply the mufta bihi ruling of permissibility.

Core Idea
Sajdat al-Shukr: Abu Hanifa said makruh, but the fatwa is permissible and recommended.

Sajdat al-Shukr, a prostration of thanks, is a practice with roots in the Prophet's sunnah. Yet within the Hanafi school, the early masters differed on its legal classification. This passage from Imdad al-Fattah presents the positions of Imam Abu Hanifa, Imam Muhammad, and the two narrations from Abu Yusuf, along with the evidence and the eventual fatwa that reconciles them. Understanding this dispute hones your skill in navigating intra-madhhab ikhtilaf and seeing how later jurists settle disagreements.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three Hanafi positions
State the views of Abu Hanifa (makruh), Abu Yusuf (two narrations: makruh and qurbah), and Muhammad (sunnah).
2
Examine the evidence for each position
Abu Hanifa argues via principle (no qurbah for less than a rak'ah except tilawah) and claims abrogation. The Sahibayn cite multiple hadiths of the Prophet prostrating when receiving good news.
3
Analyze the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: if one sleeps during the prostration, does it nullify wudu? It depends on whether it is considered a qurbah.
4
Understand the later tarjih
The author of al-Hujjah reconciles: Abu Hanifa's statement negates obligation, Muhammad's affirms permissibility and recommendation. Both are acted upon.
5
Apply the mufta bihi ruling
Today, it is permissible and recommended to perform Sajdat al-Shukr when receiving a blessing. One should not forbid others from it.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل سجدة الشكر
(سجدة الشكر مكروهة عند الإمام أبي حنيفة، رحمه الله تعالى، قال في « التاتارخانية » : وفي « القدوري عن أبي حنيفة أنه يكره سجدة الشكر انتهى. وقد رُوي عن إبراهيم النخعي: أنـه كان يكرهها، كذا في السير الكبير ، انتهى. وفي المختلف قال أبو حنيفة رحمه الله، سجدة الشكر غير مشروعة قربة، انتهى. وقال الكمال وعند أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف ما دون الركعة ليس بقربة شرعاً، إلا في محل النص وهو سجود التلاوة، فلا يكون السجود وحده قـربـة فـي غـيـره انتهى. وفي السغناقي» سجدة الشكر عند محمد مسنونة، وعند أبي حنيفة، وإحدى الروايتين عن أبي يوسف غير مسنونة انتهى. وعن محمد عن أبي حنيفة أنه كرهه، وروي عن أبي حنيفة أنه قال: لا أراه شيئاً، قيل: إنه لم يرد به نفي شرعيتها قربة، بل أراد نفي وجوبها شكراً، لعدم إحصاء نعم الله تعالى فتكون مباحة، انتهى. أو لا يراها شكراً تاماً، وتمام الشكر في صلاة ركعتين، كما فعله رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم يوم فتح مكة)، كذا في السير الكبير ) ، انتهى. وقال الأكثرون إنها ليست بقربة عنده، بـل هـي مكروهة، لا يثاب عليها وتركها أولى وقال بعضهم: هي قربة يثاب عليها، وثمرة الخلاف تظهر في انتقاض الطهارة إذا نام في سجود الشكر ، انتهى. وجه قول أبي حنيفة أن نصب الأحكام بالرأي متعذر، وما روي « أنه عليه الصلاة والسلام كان يسجد إذا رأى مبتلى ) فهو منسوخ". (وَقَالا) أي: محمد وأبو يوسف في إحدى الروايتين عنه (هي) أي: سجدة الشكر (قُرْبَةٌ يُثاب عليها)، لما روى الستة إلا النسائي عن أبي بكرة ( أن النبي لو كان إذا أتاه أمر يسره أو بشر به خر ساجداً )، وعن عبد الرحمن بن عوف: خرج صلى الله عليه وسلم نحو صدقته فاستقبل القبلة فخر ساجداً فأطال السجود ثـم رفــع رأسه، فقال: « إن جبريل عليه السلام أتاني فبشرني فقال: إن الله عز وجل يقول لك: مَنْ صَلَّى عَلَيْكَ صَلَّيْتُ عَلَيْهِ، وَمَنْ سَلَّمَ عَلَيْكَ سَلَّمْتُ عَلَيْهَ، فَسَجَدْتُ الله شكرا ) رواه أحمد.
وهيئتها مثل سجدة التلاوة فائدة مهمة؛ لدفع كلِّ نازلة مهمة، قال الإمامُ النَّسَفِي فِي الكافي: مَنْ قرأَ آيَ السجدة كلها في مجلس واحد، وسجد لكل منها، كفاه الله ما أهمه.
وعن سعد بن أبي وقاص قال: خرجنا مع النبي الله من مكة نريد المدينة، فلما كنا قريبـاً مـن عــزورا نــزل ثم رفع يديه فدعا الله ساعة، ثم خر ساجداً فعله ثلاثاً، وقال: « إِنِّي سَأَلْتُ رَبِّي وَشَفِّعْتُ لَأُمَّتِي، فَأَعْطَانِي تُلْكَ أُمَّتِي، فَخَرَرْتُ سَاجِدَاً شُكْرَاً، لِرَبِّي ثُمَّ رَفَعْتُ رَأْسِي فَسَأَلْتُ رَبِّي لأمَّتِي، فَأَعْطَانِي ثُلْتَ أَمَّتِي فَخَرَرْتُ سَاجِدَاً شكراً، ثُمَّ رَفَعْتُ رَأْسِي فَسَأَلْتُ رَبِّي لأُمَّتِي، فَأَعْطَانِي الثلث الأخير فَخَرَرْتُ سَاجِدًا لِرَبِّي ) ) رواه أبو داود، وسجد أبو بكر له حين جاءه قتل مسيلمة (۲)، رواه سعيد ، وسجد عليه حين وجدوا ذا الثدية في الخوارج 1 مقتولاً ] رواه أحمد في مسنده، وكذا رواه محمد في ( السير الكبير»، وأجاب في الله المختلف عن هذا بالنسخ ، وهذا عمل الصحابة بنفسه كذا بخط شيخ مشايخنا المقدسي رحمهم تعالى، انتهى. وفي « التاتارخانية ) قال صاحب ( الحجة » رحمه الله : عندي أن قول أبي حنيفة رحمه الله محمول على الإيجاب، وقول محمد على الجواز [ والاستحباب ](4) فيعمل بهما، لا يجب لكل نعمة سجدة شكر، كما قال أبو حنيفة، ولكن يجوز أن يسجد سجدة الشكر في وقت سُر بنعمة أو ذكر فشكرها بالسجدة، وأنه غير خارج عن حد الاستحباب، وقد ذكرت فيه روايات كثيرة عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم وعـن الصحابة والتابعين، وروي « أن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم لما أتي برأس أبي جهل – لعنه الله - يوم بدر وأُلقي بين يديه، نعمة سجد الله خمس سجدات شكراً، وقرأ آية السجدة وسورة انشقت وسجد الله عز وجل عشر سجدات الأولى للتلاوة والباقيات شكراً للمكرمات ) ()، فلا يمنع العباد عن سجدة الشكر لما فيــه مـن الخضوع والتعبد وعليه الفتوى انتهى (وهيئتها ) : أن يكبر مستقبل القبلة ويسجد فيحمد الله ويشكر ويسبح، ثم يكبر فيرفع رأسه (مثل سجدة التلاوة) بشرائطها.
(فائدة مهمة لدفع كلِّ نازلة مهمة)
« ينبغي الاهتمام بتعلمها وتعليمها. (قال) الشيخ (الإمام) حافظ الحق والملة والدين، عبد الله بن أحمد بن محمود ( النَّسَفِيُّ في كتابه : (الكَافِي) شرح الوافي : (مَنْ قرأَ آيَ السَّجدة كلها) وهي أربعة عشر آية، قد علمتها مجموعة في باب سجود التلاوة، وقصدت بجمعها تقريب الأمر لهذه الفائدة مع حكم السجود المتقدم بيانه، رجاء فضل الله ورحمته ( في مجلس واحد، وسجد) بتلاوته ( لِكُلِّ) آية (مِنْهَا) سجدة (كفاهُ اللهُ تعالى (ما أهمَّـهُ) من أمر دنياه وآخـرتـه، ونقـلـه عـنـه أيـضـاً المحقق الكمال بن الهمام بفتح القدير ) وكذا غيره من الشراح رحمهم الله تعالى.
Chapter: Sajdat al-Shukr (Prostration of Thanks)
(Sajdat al-Shukr is disliked (makruh) according to Imam Abu Hanifa, may Allah have mercy on him. He said in al-Tatarkhaniyyah: In al-Quduri from Abu Hanifa that he dislikes Sajdat al-Shukr, end. And it has been narrated from Ibrahim al-Nakha'i that he disliked it, likewise in al-Siyar al-Kabir, end. In al-Mukhtalif, Abu Hanifa said: Sajdat al-Shukr is not legislated as an act of drawing near (qurbah), end. Al-Kamal said: According to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, what is less than a rak'ah is not a qurbah legally, except in the specified place which is the prostration of recitation (sujud al-tilawah), so prostration alone is not a qurbah in other than it, end. In al-Sighnaqi: Sajdat al-Shukr according to Muhammad is sunnah, and according to Abu Hanifa and one of the two narrations from Abu Yusuf is not sunnah, end. From Muhammad from Abu Hanifa that he disliked it, and it is narrated from Abu Hanifa that he said: I do not consider it anything; it is said that by this he did not intend negation of its being legislated as a qurbah, but rather he intended negation of its obligation as thanks, due to the impossibility of enumerating the blessings of Allah Almighty, so it would be permissible (mubah), end. Or he does not consider it a complete thanks, and the complete thanks is in praying two rak'ahs, as the Messenger of Allah did on the day of the conquest of Mecca, as in al-Siyar al-Kabir, end. And the majority said that it is not a qurbah according to him, rather it is disliked, no reward for it, and its abandonment is better. And some said: it is a qurbah rewarded, and the fruit of the difference appears concerning the nullification of ritual purity (taharah) if one sleeps during the prostration of thanks, end. The argument of Abu Hanifa is that establishing rulings by personal opinion is not possible, and what is narrated that he (peace be upon him) used to prostrate when he saw an afflicted person) is abrogated.
(And the two said,) i.e., Muhammad and Abu Yusuf in one of the two narrations from him, (it,) i.e., Sajdat al-Shukr, (is a qurbah rewarded for it,) because of what the six (except al-Nasa'i) narrated from Abu Bakrah (that the Prophet, when something pleasing came to him or he was given good news, would fall prostrate), and from Abd al-Rahman ibn Awf: "He (peace be upon him) went out toward his charity, faced the qiblah, fell prostrate and prolonged the prostration, then raised his head and said: 'Indeed Jibril came to me and gave me good news saying: Allah says to you: Whoever prays upon you, I pray upon him, and whoever greets you, I greet him, so I prostrated to Allah in thanks'" narrated by Ahmad.
And its form is like the prostration of recitation. An important benefit: for repelling every important calamity. Imam al-Nasafi said in al-Kafi: "Whoever recites all the verses of prostration in one sitting, and prostrates for each of them, Allah will suffice him for what concerns him."
And from Sa'd ibn Abi Waqqas: We went out with the Prophet from Mecca intending Medina, and when we were near 'Azura, he descended then raised his hands and supplicated to Allah for an hour, then fell prostrate, doing it three times, and said: "I asked my Lord and interceded for my ummah, and He gave me one-third of my ummah, so I fell prostrate in thanks to my Lord, then I raised my head and asked my Lord for my ummah, and He gave me one-third of my ummah, so I fell prostrate in thanks, then I raised my head and asked my Lord for my ummah, and He gave me the last third, so I fell prostrate to my Lord," narrated by Abu Dawud, and Abu Bakr prostrated when the death of Musaylimah was reported to him, narrated by Sa'id, and 'Ali prostrated when they found Dhu al-Thudayyah among the Khawarij killed, narrated by Ahmad in his Musnad, and likewise Muhammad narrated in al-Siyar al-Kabir, and in al-Mukhtalif he answered this with abrogation, and this is the action of the Companions themselves, as is in the handwriting of our shaykh's shaykh al-Maqdisi, may Allah have mercy on them, end. In al-Tatarkhaniyyah, the author of al-Hujjah said: In my view, the statement of Abu Hanifa is interpreted as negating obligation, and the statement of Muhammad as permissibility [and recommendation], so both are acted upon: it is not obligatory for every blessing a prostration of thanks, as Abu Hanifa said, but it is permissible to prostrate the prostration of thanks at a time of joy for a blessing, or when mentioning it and thanking for it with prostration, and it is not outside the bounds of recommendation, and many narrations have been mentioned about this from the Prophet and from the Companions and the Successors, and it is narrated that when the head of Abu Jahl was brought to the Messenger of Allah on the day of Badr and thrown before him, he prostrated five prostrations in thanks, and he recited the verse of prostration and Surah al-Inshiqaq and prostrated to Allah ten prostrations, the first for recitation and the rest in thanks for the honors, so one should not prevent the servants from the prostration of thanks because of the humility and worship in it, and upon this is the fatwa. End. (And its form) is that he should make takbir facing the qiblah, prostrate, praise Allah, thank, and glorify, then make takbir and raise his head (like the prostration of recitation) with its conditions.
(An important benefit for repelling every important calamity): "One should pay attention to learning and teaching it." (The Shaykh) al-Imam Hafiz al-Haqq wa al-Millah wa al-Din, Abdullah ibn Ahmad ibn Mahmud (al-Nasafi) said in his book al-Kafi, commentary on al-Wafi: (Whoever recites all the verses of prostration) which are fourteen verses, and you have already known them collected in the chapter of Sujud al-Tilawah, and my intent in compiling them is to make it easier for this benefit along with the ruling of prostration previously explained, hoping for Allah's bounty and mercy, (in one session, and prostrates) through his recitation (for each) verse (of them) a prostration, (Allah Almighty will suffice him for) whatever concerns him from the matters of this world and the Hereafter. This is also narrated from him by al-Muhaqqiq Kamal ibn al-Humam in Fath al-Qadir, and likewise other commentators, may Allah have mercy on them.
Source pages p. 516

Commentary
This passage from Imdad al-Fattah, a commentary on Nur al-Idah, discusses the ruling on Sajdat al-Shukr (prostration of thanks). It begins with the position of Imam Abu Hanifa that it is makruh (disliked). The text then presents the view of the two companions, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, that it is a qurbah (act of drawing near to Allah) for which one is rewarded. The commentary provides the evidence for each position. Abu Hanifa's evidence is based on the principle that acts of worship are not established by personal opinion, and the hadiths cited are claimed to be abrogated. The Sahibayn rely on numerous hadiths showing the Prophet (peace be upon him) prostrating in thanks, including the hadith of Abu Bakrah and the story of Jibril giving glad tidings. The text then discusses the reconciliation by some later scholars: Abu Hanifa's position is interpreted as negating obligation, while Muhammad's is permissibility and recommendation. The fatwa according to later authorities is that one should not forbid Sajdat al-Shukr, as it contains humility and worship. Finally, the passage describes the form of the prostration (like sujud al-tilawah) and includes a benefit from Imam al-Nasafi about reciting all verses of prostration in one sitting and prostrating for each, for which Allah will suffice one's concerns.

Key Terms
سجدة الشكر (Sajdat al-Shukr): A prostration performed to express thanks to Allah for a blessing or good news.
مكروهة (makruhah): Disliked; according to Abu Hanifa, Sajdat al-Shukr is not a qurbah and its performance is disliked, no reward, and abandonment is better.
قربة (qurbah): An act of drawing near to Allah that is legislated (mashru') and rewarded.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, what is the ruling on Sajdat al-Shukr?
A) Sunnah
B) Makruh
C) Wajib
D) Haram

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school's internal dispute on Sajdat al-Shukr is resolved by later scholars who deem it permissible and recommended, balancing the early imams' views.

intermediate

Prostration of Thanks: Ruling and Description
Explains description of sajdat al-shukr and provides an important benefit

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the relied-upon Hanafi ruling on sajdat al-shukr and identify the intra-Hanafi dispute on its obligation.

Core Idea
Sajdat al-shukr is recommended, not obligatory, according to the relied-upon Hanafi view.

This passage from 'Imdad al-Fattah' explains the form of the prostration of thanks (sajdat al-shukr) and then presents a key legal benefit regarding reciting all sajdah verses. More importantly, it resolves an internal Hanafi dispute: is this prostration obligatory (wajib) as Abu Hanifa held, or merely recommended (mustahabb) as Muhammad al-Shaybani held? The final fatwa settles on recommendation, supported by prophetic practice and companion reports.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling level
Locate the description of sajdat al-shukr. Note its similarity to sajdat al-tilawah and the final ruling: mustahabb (recommended).
2
Recognize the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Observe that Abu Hanifa considered it wajib, while Muhammad al-Shaybani said ja'iz mustahabb. The author cites al-Tatar Khaniyyah to resolve this.
This is a difference within the school.
3
Analyze the proofs
Examine the hadith of Sa'd ibn Abi Waqqas and reports of Abu Bakr and Ali prostrating in thanks. These show the Prophet's and Companions' practice, which supports recommendation rather than obligation.
The proofs are from Sunnah and practice of the Salaf.
4
Identify the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position is that of Muhammad al-Shaybani: it is not wajib but mustahabb. The fatwa is on permissibility and recommendation.
This is the operative ruling for practice.

Source Text

وهيئتها مثل سجدة التلاوة فائدة مهمة؛ لدفع كلِّ نازلة مهمة، قال الإمامُ النَّسَفِي فِي الكافي: مَنْ قرأَ آيَ السجدة كلها في مجلس واحد، وسجد لكل منها، كفاه الله ما أهمه. وعن سعد بن أبي وقاص قال: خرجنا مع النبي الله من مكة نريد المدينة، فلما كنا قريبـاً مـن عــزورا نــزل ثم رفع يديه فدعا الله ساعة، ثم خر ساجداً فعله ثلاثاً، وقال: « إِنِّي سَأَلْتُ رَبِّي وَشَفِّعْتُ لَأُمَّتِي، فَأَعْطَانِي تُلْكَ أُمَّتِي، فَخَرَرْتُ سَاجِدَاً شُكْرَاً، لِرَبِّي ثُمَّ رَفَعْتُ رَأْسِي فَسَأَلْتُ رَبِّي لأمَّتِي، فَأَعْطَانِي ثُلْتَ أَمَّتِي فَخَرَرْتُ سَاجِدَاً شكراً، ثُمَّ رَفَعْتُ رَأْسِي فَسَأَلْتُ رَبِّي لأُمَّتِي، فَأَعْطَانِي الثلث الأخير فَخَرَرْتُ سَاجِدًا لِرَبِّي ) ) رواه أبو داود، وسجد أبو بكر له حين جاءه قتل مسيلمة ، رواه سعيد ، وسجد عليه حين وجدوا ذا الثدية في الخوارج مقتولاً ] رواه أحمد في مسنده، وكذا رواه محمد في ( السير الكبير»، وأجاب في الله المختلف عن هذا بالنسخ ، وهذا عمل الصحابة بنفسه كذا بخط شيخ مشايخنا المقدسي رحمهم تعالى، انتهى. وفي « التاتارخانية ) قال صاحب ( الحجة » رحمه الله : عندي أن قول أبي حنيفة رحمه الله محمول على الإيجاب، وقول محمد على الجواز [ والاستحباب ] فيعمل بهما، لا يجب لكل نعمة سجدة شكر، كما قال أبو حنيفة، ولكن يجوز أن يسجد سجدة الشكر في وقت سُر بنعمة أو ذكر فشكرها بالسجدة، وأنه غير خارج عن حد الاستحباب، وقد ذكرت فيه روايات كثيرة عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم وعـن الصحابة والتابعين، وروي « أن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم لما أتي برأس أبي جهل – لعنه الله - يوم بدر وأُلقي بين يديه، سجد الله خمس سجدات شكراً، وقرأ آية السجدة وسورة انشقت وسجد الله عز وجل عشر سجدات الأولى للتلاوة والباقيات شكراً للمكرمات )، فلا يمنع العباد عن سجدة الشكر لما فيــه مـن الخضوع والتعبد وعليه الفتوى انتهى (وهيئتها ) : أن يكبر مستقبل القبلة ويسجد فيحمد الله ويشكر ويسبح، ثم يكبر فيرفع رأسه (مثل سجدة التلاوة) بشرائطها. (فائدة مهمة لدفع كلِّ نازلة مهمة) « ينبغي الاهتمام بتعلمها وتعليمها. (قال) الشيخ (الإمام) حافظ الحق والملة والدين، عبد الله بن أحمد بن محمود ( النَّسَفِيُّ في كتابه : (الكَافِي) شرح الوافي : (مَنْ قرأَ آيَ السَّجدة كلها) وهي أربعة عشر آية، قد علمتها مجموعة في باب سجود التلاوة، وقصدت بجمعها تقريب الأمر لهذه الفائدة مع حكم السجود المتقدم بيانه، رجاء فضل الله ورحمته ( في مجلس واحد، وسجد) بتلاوته ( لِكُلِّ) آية (مِنْهَا) سجدة (كفاهُ اللهُ تعالى (ما أهمَّـهُ) من أمر دنياه وآخـرتـه، ونقـلـه عـنـه أيـضـاً المحقق الكمال بن الهمام بفتح القدير ) وكذا غيره من الشراح رحمهم الله تعالى.
Its description is like the prostration of recitation. An important benefit: to repel every important calamity. Imam al-Nasafi said in al-Kafi: Whoever recites all the verses of prostration in one sitting and prostrates for each, Allah suffices him in what concerns him. And from Sa'd ibn Abi Waqqas: We went out with the Prophet from Mecca heading to Madinah... [the hadith continues] ... Abu Bakr prostrated when he received news of Musaylimah's killing. Ali prostrated when they found Dhu al-Thudayyah killed among the Khawarij. The response to the difference on this is abrogation... In al-Tatar Khaniyyah, the author of al-Hujjah said: In my view, Abu Hanifa's statement is interpreted as obligation, and Muhammad's statement as permissibility and recommendation; so both are applied. It is not obligatory to prostrate for every blessing as Abu Hanifa said, but it is permissible to prostrate in gratitude when delighted by a blessing or remembrance... The relied-upon fatwa is that. And its description: to say takbir facing the qibla, prostrate, praise Allah and give thanks and glorify, then say takbir and raise the head, like the prostration of recitation with its conditions. An important benefit to repel every important calamity: It is recommended to pay attention to learning and teaching it. Al-Nasafi said: Whoever recites all the verses of prostration—which are fourteen—in one sitting and prostrates for each, Allah suffices him in what concerns him of his worldly and afterlife affairs. This was also transmitted by al-Kamal ibn al-Humam in Fath al-Qadir and other commentators.
Source pages p. 517

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on the prostration of thanks (sajdat al-shukr). The author begins by stating that its description is identical to that of the prostration of recitation (sajdat al-tilawah). After explaining the form, he introduces an important benefit (fā'idah) concerning reciting all fourteen verses of prostration in one sitting. The benefit is narrated from Imam al-Nasafi in al-Kafi, promising divine sufficiency to the one who does so. The author then provides a long hadith from Sa'd ibn Abi Waqqas describing the Prophet's repeated prostrations of thanks when his supplication for his ummah was granted. This is followed by reports of Abu Bakr and Ali prostrating in thanks upon joyous events. The author then addresses an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf: Abu Hanifa held sajdat al-shukr to be wajib (obligatory), while Muhammad al-Shaybani held it to be merely permissible and recommended (mustahabb). The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that of Muhammad: it is mustahabb, not wajib. The passage closes by repeating the description of the prostration: one faces the qibla, says takbir, prostrates, offers praise and thanks, then rises with takbir, fulfilling the same conditions as sajdat al-tilawah. Finally, the benefit is re-emphasized: learning and teaching this practice is recommended.

Key Terms
سجدة الشكر (sajdat al-shukr): Prostration performed as an expression of gratitude to Allah upon receiving a blessing or being saved from a calamity.
سجدة التلاوة (sajdat al-tilawah): Prostration performed upon reciting or hearing a verse of prostration from the Quran.
استحباب (istihbāb): The legal category of recommended actions; performing them is rewarded, but omitting them is not sinful.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the relied-upon (mufta bihi) ruling on sajdat al-shukr according to the text?
A) Wajib
B) Mustahabb
C) Haram
D) Makruh

Key Takeaway
Sajdat al-shukr is mustahabb (recommended) in the Hanafi school, not wajib; it is a virtuous act of gratitude.

Friday Prayer: Definition and Obligation (Fard 'Ayn)
Introduces chapter on Friday prayer, defines term, and states ruling as fard 'ayn with proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the linguistic derivation of the term 'Jumu'ah' and explain why Friday prayer is fard 'ayn using the Quranic verse and hadith proofs.

Core Idea
Friday prayer is an individual obligation (fard 'ayn) established by Quran, Sunnah, and consensus; its denial is disbelief.

This lesson introduces the chapter on Friday prayer. We begin with the linguistic meaning of 'Jumu'ah', derived from social gathering. The author then emphatically states that Friday prayer is fard 'ayn — an individual obligation — and supports it with the Quranic command to hasten to the remembrance of Allah on Friday and with multiple hadiths warning against neglect.

Guided Path
1
Identify the linguistic roots
Note the derivation of 'Jumu'ah' from 'ijtimā'' (gathering) and the variations in pronunciation (sukun, ḍammah, fatḥ) across Arabic dialects.
The passage details dialectical differences and even notes the plural forms.
2
Extract the core ruling
The passage explicitly states 'Friday prayer is fard 'ayn' and warns that its denier becomes a disbeliever, indicating the strength of the obligation.
This sets the legal weight: it is a definite individual obligation.
3
Analyze the primary proof: Quran 62:9
The imperative 'fas'aw' (hasten) indicates obligation. The 'remembrance of Allah' is interpreted as either the prayer or the sermon; both readings lead to the obligation of Friday prayer.
The commentary explains that even if 'dhikr' refers to the sermon, hastening to a condition implies the obligation of the conditioned (the prayer).
4
Examine the secondary proofs: Hadiths
The hadiths list exempted persons (slave, woman, child, sick, traveler) and prescribe severe consequences for missing three consecutive Friday prayers without excuse, up to sealing of the heart.
These hadiths reinforce the fard 'ayn status and show that only specific excuses excuse one from attending.
5
Summarize the evidence
The obligation is established by the Quran (definitive text), multiple hadiths (mutawātir in meaning), and consensus (ijmā'). Denying it leads to takfīr.
Thus, Friday prayer is a foundational act of worship in Islam.

Source Text

باب الجمعة صلاة الجمعة فرضُ عَيْنٍ. باب الجمعة هي من الاجتماع، كالنجعة من الانتجاع، وهو طلب الكلأ ، بسكون الميم في استعمال أهـل اللسان، والقراء يضمونها، وفتحها حكاه الفراء والواحدي وفي المصباح» : ضم الميم لغة الحجاز، وفتحها لغة تميم، وإسكانها لغة عقيل وقرأ بها الأعمش والجمع جمع وجمعات، مثل غرف وغرفات في وجوههما انتهى، أضيف إليها اليوم والصلاة، ثم كثر الاستعمال حتـى حـذف منـهـا الدراية». (صلاة الجمعة فرضُ عَيْن)، اعلم أن الجمعة فريضة محكمة بالكتاب والسنة والإجماع، ونوع من المعنى، فيكفر جاحدها، قال تعالى: ﴿يَتأَيُّهَا الَّذِينَ ءَامَنُوا إِذَا نُودِيَ لِلصَّلَوَةِ مِن يَوْمِ الْجُمُعَةِ فَاسْعَوْا [ال : ٩] رتب الأمر بالسعي للذكر على النداء فالظاهر المراد بالذكر الصلاة، ويجوز كون المراد به الخطبة، وعلى كل تقدير يفيد افتراض الجمعة فالأول ظاهر، والثاني كذلك، لأن افتراض السعي إلى الشرط وهو المقصود لغيره فرع افتراض ذلك الغير، وقال عليه الصلاة والسلام: الْجُمُعَةُ حَقٌّ وَاجِبٌ عَلَى كُلِّ مُسْلِمٍ فِي جَمَاعَةٍ إِلا أَرْبَعَةٌ: عَبْدٌ مَمْلُوكُ أَوْ امْرَأَةٌ أَوْ صَبِيٌّ أَوْ مريض ) وفي ( البخاري » : « إِلا عَلَى صَبِي أَوْ مَمْلُوكٍ أَوْ مُسَافِر » ورواه الطبراني وزاد فيـــه: ( المَرْأةُ والمَرِيضُ )، وقال عليه الصلاة والسلام في حديث: «وَاعْلَمُوا أَنَّ اللَّهَ قَدْ أَفَتَرَضَ عَلَيْكُمْ الْجُمُعَةَ فِي يَوْمِي هَذَا، فِي شَهْرِي هَذَا، فِي مَقَامِي هَذَا، فَمَنْ تَرَكَهَا تَهَاؤُنَا بِهَا، وَاسْتِحْفَافًا بِحَفْهَا، وَلَهُ إِمَامٌ عَادِلٌ أَوْ جَائِرٌ، ألا وَلا جَمَعَ اللهُ لَهُ شَمْلَهُ، وَلا بَارَكَ لَهُ فِي أمْرِهِ، ألا وَلا صَلاةَ لَهُ، وَلَا زَكَاةَ لَهُ، وَلا حَجَّ لَهُ، وَلا صَوْمَ لَهُ، إلا أنْ يَتُوبَ ، فَمَنْ تَابَ تَابَ اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ » )، وفي رواية قال: « فَرِيْضَةٌ وَاجِبَةٌ إلى يَوْمِ القِيَامَةِ ، وقال : ( مَنْ تَرَكَ ثَلاثَ جُمَعِ مُتَوَالِيَاتٍ مِنْ غَيْرِ عُدْرٍ طَبَعَ اللَّهُ عَلَى قَلْبِهِ، وَمَنْ يَطْبَعِ اللَّهُ عَلَى قَلْبِهِ يَجْعَلُهُ فِي أَسْفَلِ دَرَكِ جَهَنَّمَ ) وقال أيضاً: «مَنْ تَرَكَ ثَلَاثَ جَمُعَاتٍ مِنْ غَيْرِ
Chapter of Friday: Friday prayer is an individual obligation. Chapter of Friday: It is derived from social gathering, like al-naj'ah from al-intijā' (seeking pasture). The letter mīm is sukun according to linguists, but readers make it ḍammah. Fatḥ was narrated by al-Farrā' and al-Wāḥidī. In al-Miṣbāḥ: ḍamm of mīm is the Ḥijāzī dialect, fatḥ is Tamīmī, sukun is 'Aqīlī, and al-A'mash recited it. The plural is jumu' and jumu'āt like ghuruf and ghurufāt. The word was added to 'day' and 'prayer', then usage increased until the added word was deleted. (Friday prayer is individual obligation). Know that Friday is an established obligation by the Book, Sunnah, and consensus, and its denier becomes a disbeliever. Allah said: 'O you who have believed, when the call is made for prayer on the day of Jumu'ah, then hasten to the remembrance of Allah.' He linked the command to hasten to the remembrance with the call, so the apparent meaning of 'remembrance' is the prayer, and it is also possible it means the sermon. In either case, it indicates the obligation of Friday prayer. The first interpretation is apparent, and the second also, because making haste to a condition (the sermon) to achieve the intended (prayer) is dependent on the obligation of that intended. The Prophet said: 'Friday is a due right obligatory upon every Muslim in congregation, except four: a slave, a woman, a child, or a sick person.' In al-Bukhārī: 'except a child, a slave, or a traveler.' Al-Ṭabrānī added: 'the woman and the sick.' And the Prophet said: 'Know that Allah has made Friday prayer obligatory upon you on this day, in this month, in this place of mine; so whoever leaves it out of laziness and disregard while having a just or unjust leader, then Allah will not unite his affairs, nor bless him in his matter. Truly, there is no prayer, no zakah, no hajj, no fasting for him, unless he repents; and whoever repents, Allah turns to him.' In another narration: 'An obligatory duty until the Day of Judgment.' And he said: 'Whoever leaves three Friday prayers consecutively without an excuse, Allah seals his heart, and whoever Allah seals his heart, He puts him in the lowest level of Hell.' And he also said: 'Whoever leaves three Friday prayers without...'
Source pages p. 518

Commentary
This passage begins the chapter on Friday prayer (Bāb al-Jumu'ah). The author first provides a linguistic analysis of the word 'Jumu'ah', noting its derivation from social gathering and the various dialectical pronunciations. He then states the ruling: 'Friday prayer is an individual obligation (fard 'ayn).' This is elaborated by asserting its firm establishment through the Quran, Sunnah, and consensus; denying it constitutes disbelief (takfīr). The primary proof is the Quranic verse in Sūrat al-Jumu'ah: 'O you who have believed, when the call is made for prayer on the day of Jumu'ah, then hasten to the remembrance of Allah.' The author explains that the command to 'hasten to the remembrance' proves the obligation of Friday prayer, whether the 'remembrance' refers to the prayer itself or the sermon. The argument is that if the remembrance is the prayer, the obligation is direct; if it is the sermon, hastening to a condition implies the obligation of the conditioned (the prayer). The passage then cites multiple hadiths to reinforce the obligation. The first hadith lists those exempt from the obligation: slave, woman, child, sick, and according to al-Bukhārī's version, a traveler. Severe warnings are given against abandoning Jumu'ah, including sealing of the heart and punishment in Hell. The passage ends abruptly while quoting the hadith about three consecutive missed Friday prayers.

Key Terms
الجمعة (al-jumu'ah): The Friday congregational prayer that replaces the Zuhr prayer, consisting of two rak'ahs and a khutbah, made obligatory on qualified Muslims.
فرض عين (fard 'ayn): An individual obligation incumbent on every qualified Muslim; neglecting it without excuse is sinful.

B) Surah al-Jumu'ah 62:9

D) Surah al-Ma'un 107:4

Key Takeaway
Friday prayer is a definitive individual obligation (fard 'ayn) established by Quran, multiple hadiths, and consensus; abandoning it without excuse invites severe punishment.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
15 min
Friday Prayer: Obligation and Conditions
Explains the ruling of Friday prayer as fard 'ayn with proofs and conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling of Friday prayer as fard 'ayn and identify the seven conditions for its obligation, citing the key proofs (Quran, hadith, ijma, rational).

Core Idea
Friday prayer is fard 'ayn: its denial is disbelief, and it is more emphatic than Dhuhr.

Friday prayer is one of the most distinctive acts of worship in Islam, a weekly congregation that unites the community. This lesson establishes its obligation as fard 'ayn (individual duty) from the Quran, Sunnah, consensus, and rational proof, and then outlines the seven conditions that must be met for it to be obligatory. Understanding both the ruling and its conditions is essential for proper practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core ruling
The author states that Friday prayer is fard 'ayn (individual obligation). Note that the Hanafi school considers its denial as kufr (disbelief).
This is the foundational claim of the passage.
2
Trace the Quranic proof
The verse (al-Jumu'ah 9) commands proceeding to the remembrance of Allah after the call. The commentator explains that 'remembrance' likely refers to the prayer or the sermon, both leading to obligation.
The imperative (amr) indicates obligation in Hanafi usul.
3
Examine the hadith proofs
Multiple hadiths are cited: one listing exceptions (slave, woman, child, sick), another threatening abandonment, and a third linking neglect to hypocrisy.
These hadiths reinforce the mandatory nature.
4
Understand the rational proof
We are commanded to leave Dhuhr for Friday; since Dhuhr is fard, leaving it is only permissible for a more emphatic obligation, proving Friday's greater weight.
This is an argument from necessity (al-darurah).
5
List the seven conditions
The conditions are: masculinity, freedom, residence (not traveling), being in a city (misr), sanity, adulthood, and health (implied by the hadith exceptions).
Women, slaves, travelers, villagers, children, insane, and sick are exempt.

Chapter of Friday. Friday prayer is an individual obligation (fard 'ayn). Chapter of Friday. It is derived from 'social gathering', like 'al-naj'ah' from 'al-intija'' which means seeking pasture. The letter mim is sakina in the usage of the people of language, and readers of Quran pronounce it with dammah, and fatha was narrated by al-Farra' and al-Wahidi. In al-Misbah: pronouncing the mim with dammah is the language of Hijaz, with fatha is the language of Tamim, and with sukun is the language of 'Uqayl, and al-A'mash recited it with sukun. The plural is jumu' and jumu'at, like ghuruf and ghurufat in their forms. End quote. The day and the prayer were added to it, then usage became abundant until the added part was omitted, as in al-Dirayah. (Friday prayer is fard 'ayn): Know that Friday is an established obligation by the Book, the Sunnah, and consensus, and also a type of rational meaning. Its denier is declared a disbeliever. Allah Most High said: 'O you who have believed, when [the call to] prayer is announced on the day of Jumu'ah [Friday], then proceed to the remembrance of Allah...' [al-Jumu'ah: 9]. He ordered proceeding to remembrance upon the call. The apparent meaning of 'remembrance' is the prayer, and it is also possible that it means the sermon. In either case, it indicates the obligation of Friday prayer. The first interpretation is apparent; the second is also such because the obligation of proceeding to the condition, which is intended for something else, is a derivative of the obligation of that thing. And the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'Friday is a right and duty upon every Muslim in congregation except four: an owned slave, a woman, a child, or a sick person.' And in al-Bukhari: 'except upon a child, a slave, or a traveler.' And al-Tabarani narrated it and added: 'the woman and the sick.' And the Prophet (peace be upon him) said in a hadith: 'Know that Allah has made Friday obligatory upon you on this day of mine, in this month of mine, in this place of mine. Whoever abandons it out of neglect and disrespect, while he has a just or unjust ruler, then may Allah not gather his affairs, nor bless him in his matter; indeed, no prayer, no zakat, no hajj, no fasting for him except if he repents; then if he repents, Allah relents upon him.' And in another narration: 'An obligatory duty until the Day of Judgment.' And he said: 'Whoever leaves three consecutive Friday prayers without an excuse, Allah seals his heart, and whoever Allah seals his heart, He places him in the lowest level of Hell.' And he also said: 'Whoever leaves three Friday prayers without an excuse is written among the hypocrites.' As for consensus: Muslims from the time of the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) to this day have agreed upon its obligation without any denial. It is fard 'ayn except according to Ibn Kaj from the Shafi'i school, who says it is fard kifayah, which is an error, mentioned in al-Hilyah from their books. And as for rational meaning: We are commanded to leave Dhuhr for the establishment of Friday, and Dhuhr is an obligation. It is not permissible to leave an obligation except for a more emphasized and prior obligation. Thus it indicates that Friday is more emphasized than Dhuhr in obligation. And we have increased in evidence somewhat because of what we heard from some ignorant people attributing to the Hanafi school its non-obligation. The source of their error is what was mentioned in al-Quduri: Whoever prays Dhuhr on Friday in his home without an excuse, it is disapproved (makruh) for him but his prayer is valid. But what was meant is that it is forbidden (haram) for him, and his Dhuhr is valid; the prohibition is due to leaving the obligation which is Friday, and the validity of Dhuhr is due to the existence of the time for the original obligation. However, it is suspended: if he proceeds to Friday, his Dhuhr becomes invalid, as we will mention. And you have learned that Friday is a more emphasized obligation than Dhuhr, and you have learned that its denier is declared a disbeliever from al-'Inayah, al-Dirayah, al-Burhan, and Fath al-Qadir. It is fard 'ayn upon every person in whom seven conditions are found: (1) masculinity: thus women are excluded, even though the general address 'O you who have believed' includes them, but it is specified by the verse 'And stay in your homes' [al-Ahzab: 33]; (2) freedom: thus slaves are excluded; (3) residence (iqamah): thus the traveler is excluded; (4) and that the residence be in a city (misr): thus the resident in a village is excluded, based on what we narrated: Hudhayfah said: 'There is no Friday upon the people of villages; Friday is only upon the people of major cities.' And the statement of 'Ali: 'No Friday, no Eid prayer on the day of sacrifice or breaking the fast, except in a comprehensive city (misr jami') or a large town.' al-Zayla'i and others mentioned it. al-Kamal said: 'The statement of 'Ali is sufficient as an authority.' And the author of al-Hidayah traced it to the Prophet, and Ibn Hazm authenticated it. And it is not transmitted from the Companions that when they conquered lands they occupied themselves with setting up pulpits and Friday prayers except in major cities, not in villages. Had it been so, it would have been transmitted even as solitary reports. Therefore, residence in a city (misr) is necessary. Or (the condition is) residence in a place that is within the boundary of residence of the city (i.e., the area where one who leaves it with the intention of travel becomes a traveler, and one who arrives becomes a resident). This is narrated from Abu Hanifah and is the saying of Abu Yusuf, so the place is considered where whoever leaves it with the intention of travel becomes a traveler, and whoever arrives becomes a resident. This is the most authentic (asahh), because its obligation is specific to the people of the city, as we have explained, and those outside this boundary are not its people in reality or legally. And in the apparent narration (Zahir al-Riwayah) it is not obligatory upon...
Source pages p. 518

Commentary
This passage is from the commentary on the chapter of Friday prayer. It begins by defining the linguistic derivation of 'Jumu'ah' and then states the ruling: Friday prayer is fard 'ayn (individual obligation). The commentator then provides extensive proofs:

1. From the Quran: Allah's command 'proceed to the remembrance of Allah' after the call on Friday. The commentator argues that 'remembrance' refers to the prayer or the sermon, both implying obligation. The command indicates wujub.

2. From the Sunnah: Multiple hadiths are cited: a hadith listing exceptions (slave, woman, child, sick); a hadith threatening those who leave it; a hadith that abandoning three Friday prayers without excuse results in being written among hypocrites.

3. Consensus (ijma): The entire Muslim ummah has agreed on its obligation.

4. Rational proof (ma'na): We are commanded to leave Dhuhr for Friday. Since Dhuhr is obligatory, leaving it is only permitted for a more emphatic obligation, thus Friday is more emphatic.

Addressing a common misconception: Some ignorant people claim that the Hanafi school does not consider Friday obligatory, citing al-Quduri's statement that if one prays Dhuhr at home on Friday without excuse, it is 'disapproved' (makruh) but valid. The commentator clarifies that 'makruh' here means haram, but the Dhuhr prayer is valid because its time is still present. However, such a Dhuhr is suspended: if the person then attends Friday, the Dhuhr becomes invalid. The ruling thus affirms obligation.

Then the seven conditions for Friday prayer to be obligatory are enumerated:
1. Masculinity (dhukurah): women are exempt based on the verse 'And stay in your homes'.
2. Freedom: slaves are exempt.
3. Residence (iqamah): travelers are exempt.
4. Residence in a city (misr): residents of villages are exempt, based on athar from Hudhayfah and 'Ali.
5. (Implicitly) Sanity and adulthood: though not explicitly listed here, they are understood from the exceptions of child and sick in hadith.

The commentator further discusses the definition of 'misr' (city) and its boundary: according to Abu Hanifah and Abu Yusuf, it is the area where departure with intention of travel makes one a traveler. This is the relied-upon position (asahh). The passage concludes noting that in Zahir al-Riwayah, Friday is not obligatory on those outside this boundary.

Key Terms
الجمعة (al-jumu'ah): The Friday congregational prayer, derived from 'ijtima'' (gathering).
فرض عين (fard 'ayn): An individual obligation incumbent upon every qualified Muslim; neglecting it is sinful.
مصر (misr): A major city or urban area where Friday prayer is established; also the boundary area considered part of the city for residence.
موقوف (mawquf): Suspended; used here to describe a Dhuhr prayer that is valid initially but becomes invalid if one later attends Friday.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling of Friday prayer for a free adult male residing in a city?
A) Sunnah mu'akkadah
B) Fard kifayah
C) Fard 'ayn
D) Mubah

Key Takeaway
Friday prayer is fard 'ayn upon every Muslim who meets the seven conditions; its denial is disbelief, and its neglect is a major sin.

Seven Conditions for Obligation of Jumu'ah Prayer
Explains conditions for Jumu'ah obligation and an intra-Hanafi dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the seven conditions that make Jumu'ah fard 'ayn and identify which condition is disputed within the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Jumu'ah is fard 'ayn only on those meeting seven conditions; a blind person's obligation depends on the availability of a guide.

This passage from Imdad al-Fattah establishes the confirmed obligation of Jumu'ah and enumerates its seven conditions, addressing a common misconception that the Hanafi school denies its obligation. The author cites proofs from Qur'an, Sunnah, Ijma', and reason, then details each condition, including an important intra-Hanafi difference on whether blindness exempts a person who can find a guide.

Guided Path
1
Identify the overall ruling on Jumu'ah
The text begins by affirming that Jumu'ah is fard 'ayn, more emphatic than Zuhr, and refutes a mistaken attribution to the Hanafi school. Confirm this ruling and note the evidence used.
The author uses Qur'an, hadith, ijma', and rational argument.
2
List the seven conditions
Extract the seven conditions from the text: masculinity, freedom, residence in a city (miṣr), health, safety from an oppressor, soundness of eyesight, and the implied condition of being free from a valid excuse (which is not explicitly numbered but appears in the introductory phrase).
Only six are explicitly listed; the seventh is understood from the opening line 'upon whom seven conditions are found'.
3
Analyze the proof for each condition
For each condition, identify the scriptural or rational basis mentioned: for example, women are excluded by verse 33:33, slaves by the principle of freedom, villagers by hadith and practice of the Companions.
Pay special attention to the detailed discussion of what constitutes a miṣr.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi dispute on blindness
The text states that Abu Hanifah exempts a blind person even if a guide is available, while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad require attendance if a guide exists. Understand the basis of each view.
Later Hanafi fatwa adopts the view of the two companions (the Sahibayn).
5
Determine the mufta bihi position
The text does not explicitly give a tarjih for the blind person, but later Hanafi practice follows Abu Yusuf and Muhammad. For the definition of miṣr, the text uses 'في الأصح' indicating the preponderant view.
The mufta bihi is that Jumu'ah is obligatory on a blind person with a guide.

Upon whom seven conditions are found: masculinity, freedom, residence in a city, or within what is included in the limit of residence therein, according to the most correct view. ... (And) the fourth condition: health – by which the sick are excluded based on what we narrated. (And) the fifth: safety from an oppressor – so it is not obligatory upon one who hides from an oppressor. (And) the sixth: soundness of the two eyes – so it is not obligatory upon the blind according to Abu Hanifah, contrary to his two companions if he finds a guide to take him, and upon this difference is one who is unable.
Source pages p. 519

Commentary
This passage from Imdad al-Fattah explains the seven conditions for Jumu'ah being fard 'ayn. The author first establishes that Jumu'ah is a confirmed obligation (fard) by Qur'an, Sunnah, Ijma', and reason, refuting a mistaken attribution to the Hanafi school. He then lists the seven conditions: (1) masculinity – excluding women (specified from the general address by Qur'an 33:33); (2) freedom – excluding slaves; (3) residence in a city (mصر) – excluding villagers, supported by hadith from Hudhayfah and 'Ali; (4) health – excluding the sick, with the elderly weak appended; (5) safety from an oppressor – including the bankrupt fearing imprisonment; (6) soundness of eyes – the blind are exempt according to Abu Hanifah, while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad require attendance if a guide is available; (7) a seventh condition is implied but the text cuts off; from the beginning it appears to be 'being free from excuse' but here the author enumerates only six. The passage also thoroughly discusses the definition of 'mصر' and its annexes, stating that villages and outlying areas are not included, and that distance measured by bow-shot or miles is irrelevant. The relied-upon position is that Jumu'ah is only obligatory on residents of the city proper or its contiguous built-up area.

Key Terms
الذكورة (al-dhukūrah): Masculinity; one of the conditions for Jumu'ah obligation, excluding women.
مصر (miṣr): A large city or metropolis that has a ruler and judge, and where congregational prayers are established.
سلامة العينين (salāmat al-ʿaynayn): Soundness of both eyes; blindness exempts one from Jumu'ah according to Abu Hanifah, but not according to his two companions if a guide is available.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Jumu'ah is fard 'ayn on every free, healthy, sighted male residing in a city without fear of oppression; a blind person's obligation depends on the availability of a guide according to the relied-upon view.

Ruling on Praying Four Rak'ahs After Jumu'ah as Precaution
Intra-Hanafi dispute on praying dhuhr after Jumu'ah as ihtiyat

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the mufta bihi Hanafi position on praying four rak'ahs after Jumu'ah and explain the reasoning behind discouraging public performance.

Core Idea
Public performance of four rak'ahs after Jumu'ah is discouraged due to corruption; private performance is allowed for cautious individuals.

This passage addresses a practical concern: after Friday prayer, some Hanafis used to pray four rak'ahs as a precaution (ihtiyat) in case the Friday prayer was invalid. However, later scholars argued that this practice, if done publicly, causes corruption (mafsadah) because laypeople may misunderstand. We will examine the arguments and the mufta bihi position.

Guided Path
1
State the mufta bihi position
Identify the relied-upon ruling: it is not obligatory, and it is discouraged to perform it publicly. The discouraged status is due to the corruption it causes.
The passage emphasizes 'not to publicize' and 'not to give fatwa to the common people'.
2
Identify the opposing view
Some Hanafi mashayikh (e.g., of Marw) and a position attributed to Abu Yusuf under doubt consider it wajib or recommended as a precaution.
This opposing view is based on the weak opinion that multiple Jumu'ahs are not permitted.
3
Examine the Hanafi proof
The Hanafi response relies on the principle that precaution must be based on the stronger proof (dalil aqwa). The stronger proof here is the absolute permissibility of multiple Jumu'ahs, and prohibition would cause hardship.
The principle of ihtiyat: act on the strongest evidence, not on doubt.
4
Analyze the corruption argument
The passage details the 'great corruption': laypeople either neglect Jumu'ah thinking it is not obligatory, or mistakenly believe both Jumu'ah and dhuhr are obligatory.
This corruption outweighs the benefit of precaution.
5
Determine the practical ruling
For those who still wish to perform it out of caution (e.g., due to doubt about a condition), they should do so secretly at home without publicizing it.
The intention should be 'the last dhuhr' ensuring the prayer counts as obligation or nafl as needed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تنبيه آخر في بيان صلاة أربع بعد الجمعة بنية آخر ظهر عليه: قال الشيخ زين: ما في القنية من أمر مشايخ مرو بأداء أربع ركعات بعد الجمعة حتماً احتياطاً، مبني على القول [الضعيف] المخالف للمذهب، وهو منع جواز تعدد الجمعة فليس الاحتياط في فعلها، لأن الاحتياط العمل بأقوى الدليلين، وهو إطلاق الجواز وفي المنع حرج، وهو مدفوع، وفي فعل الأربع مفسدة عظيمة، وهي اعتقاد الجهلة أن الجمعة ليست فرضاً؛ لما يشاهدون من صلاة الظهر فيتكاسلون عن أداء الجمعة، يعني: أو اعتقادهم افتراض الجمعة والظهر بعد الجمعة أيضاً، وقد شوهد الآن صلاتها بالجماعة والإقامة لها، ونيتهم فرض الظهر الحاضر إماماً ومؤتماً بغالب المساجد، والخطيب إمامها بعد إمامته بالجمعة والجماعة وهو ظاهر الشناعة، ثم قال الشيخ زين وعلى تقدير فعلها ممن لا يخاف عليه مفسدة منها، يفعلها في بيته خفية، خوفاً من مفسدة فعلها، انتهى. وقال الشيخ العلامة علي المقدسي في نور الشمعة بعد نقله ما يفيد النهي عنها، نقول: إنما نهي عنها إذا أُديت بعد الجمعة بوصف الجماعة أو الاشتهار، ونحن لا نقول به في شيء من الأمصار، ونقول أيضاً: نحن لا نفتي العوام بهذا أي: بفعلها أصلاً بل ندل عليه الخواص، ولو بالنسبة إليهم الذين يحتاطون لأمور دينهم، ويتركون ما يريبهم إلى تحصيل يقينهم، ثم نقل عن ابن الشحنة أنه قال: لا يجب على من صلى الجمعة أن يصلي الظهر بعدها. ولا قال بذلك أحد من العلماء في علمي، وما روي عن بعض أصحابنا: أنه يستحب إن خاف عدم الإجزاء لتوهمه فوات شرط من شرائط الجمعة أن يصلي بعدها أربع [فلذلك] لا نقول أنها الظهر، ولا نوجب على ذلك بل نستحسنه احتياطاً، ولا نتظاهر به خشية توهم العوام ما وقعوا فيه من الوهم، قلت: يتعين تقييده بما قال حفيده أنه عند مجرد التوهم، أما عند قيام الشك والاشتباه في صحته، وعلى قول من يعتقد قول أبي يوسف فالظاهر وجوب الأربع، ويؤيده تعميم التمرتاشي بلابد، وغير ذلك، فتفعل بعد الجمعة، وتقدم على سنة الجمعة على ما في القنية، وفي الظهيرية: بعدها، ويقرأ في كل الأربع بفاتحة الكتاب وسورة، وقيل: في الأوليين، ويصلي على النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم في الجلوس الأخير، ولا يأتي في الثالثة بدعاء الاستفتاح، ولا تفسد بترك القعدة الأولى، وكيفية نيتها أن يقول: أصلي آخر ظهر أدركت وقته ولم أصله بعد، فيكون الاحتياط بوقوعه فرضاً آخر إن لم تصح الجمعة، وإسقاط آخر فرض ظهر عليه غيره، إن صحت، ووقوعه نفلاً إن لم يكن بذمته ظهر، والجمعة صحيحة، انتهى. ملخصاً.
Another note explaining the prayer of four [rak'ahs] after Friday [prayer] with the intention of the last dhuhr upon him: Shaykh Zayn said: What is in al-Qunyah regarding the command of the mashayikh of Marw to perform four rak'ahs after Friday [prayer] definitely as a precaution is based on the weak opinion contrary to the madhhab, which is the prohibition of the permissibility of multiple Friday prayers. So the precaution is not in performing it, because precaution is acting upon the stronger of the two proofs, which is the absolute permissibility, and in prohibition is hardship, and it is rejected, and in performing the four is a great corruption, which is the belief of the ignorant that Friday [prayer] is not obligatory; because they see the dhuhr prayer and thus become lazy in performing Friday prayer, meaning: or their belief in the obligation of Friday and also dhuhr after Friday, and it has been seen now its performance in congregation and establishing iqamah for it, and their intention is the present obligatory dhuhr, imam and followers in most mosques, and the khatib is its imam after his imamate for Friday and the congregation, and it is clearly reprehensible. Then Shaykh Zayn said: And if it is performed by one who does not fear corruption from it, he performs it in his house secretly, out of fear of the corruption of performing it, end. And Shaykh al-Allamah Ali al-Maqdisi said in Nur al-Shum'ah after quoting what indicates prohibition of it: We say: It is only prohibited when performed after Friday in the manner of congregation or publicity, and we do not say that in any of the cities, and we also say: We do not give fatwa to the common people with this i.e., performing it at all, but we indicate it to the elite, and even for them who are cautious in their religious affairs and leave what makes them doubtful to attain their certainty. Then he quoted from Ibn al-Shihnah that he said: It is not obligatory for one who performed Friday prayer to pray dhuhr after it. And no scholar said that in my knowledge. And what is narrated from some of our companions: That it is recommended if he fears lack of acceptance due to his imagining the loss of a condition of the conditions of Friday to pray four after it. Therefore we do not say it is dhuhr, nor do we make it obligatory upon that, but we consider it good as a precaution, and we do not publicize it for fear of the common people falling into the delusion they have fallen into. I said: It is necessary to restrict it to what his grandson said that it is at the time of mere imagination, but at the time of doubt and uncertainty about its validity, and according to the one who believes the statement of Abu Yusuf, the apparent is the obligation of the four, and it is supported by the generalization of al-Tamartashi necessarily and other than that. So it is performed after Friday, and given precedence over the sunnah of Friday according to what is in al-Qunyah, and in al-Zahiriyyah: after it. And he recites in each of the four Fatihah and a surah, and it is said in the first two, and he sends blessings on the Prophet in the last sitting, and does not recite the opening supplication in the third, and it is not invalidated by leaving the first sitting. And the manner of its intention is that he says: I pray the last dhuhr whose time has reached and I have not prayed it after, so the precaution is that it occurs as another obligation if Friday is not valid, and as the cancellation of the last obligatory dhuhr upon him other than it, if it is valid, and its occurrence as nafal if there is no dhuhr upon his responsibility, and Friday is valid. End. Summarized.
Source pages p. 522

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the practice of performing four rak'ahs after the Friday prayer with the intention of the last dhuhr as a precaution (ihtiyat). The author presents several scholarly opinions. Shaykh Zayn criticizes the practice as based on a weak opinion (contradicting the madhhab) and highlights the great corruption it causes: laypeople mistakenly believe Friday prayer is not obligatory when they see dhuhr being performed, or they think both Friday and dhuhr are obligatory. He allows it only for those who are not subject to such corruption, and even then it should be done secretly at home. Shaykh Ali al-Maqdisi further restricts it: the prohibition applies only if performed publicly; in private it may be allowed for cautious individuals. Ibn al-Shihnah states that it is not obligatory, and some Hanafi scholars consider it merely recommended if one imagines a condition of Friday was missed. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that it is not to be publicized or prescribed for the common people. However, if there is genuine doubt about the validity of Friday (e.g., according to Abu Yusuf), it may become obligatory. The passage concludes with detailed instructions on how to perform it (recitation, blessings, intention). The intention is key: the prayer is intended to cover the last dhuhr if Friday was invalid, or as nafal if Friday was valid. The overall thrust is that the practice is discouraged due to the potential misunderstanding it causes among the masses.

Key Terms
احتياط (ihtiyat): Precautionary action in worship to ensure fulfillment of obligation in case of doubt.
جمعة (jumu'ah): The Friday congregational prayer, a fard kifayah in Hanafi fiqh.
ظهر (zuhr): The noon obligatory prayer; here used for the precautionary prayer after Jumu'ah.
نية (niyyah): Intention; specific intention to pray 'the last dhuhr' as ihtiyat.
مفسدة (mafsadah): Corruption or harm; here referring to the negative consequence of laypeople misunderstanding the ruling.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the primary reason for discouraging the public performance of four rak'ahs after Jumu'ah?
A) It is not allowed to pray any nafil after Jumu'ah.
B) It causes laypeople to believe Jumu'ah is not obligatory or that both prayers are obligatory.
C) The Prophet explicitly prohibited it.
D) It requires a special intention that most people cannot make.

Key Takeaway
The mufta bihi Hanafi position discourages public performance of four rak'ahs after Jumu'ah as ihtiyat due to the mafsadah it causes; private performance is allowed only for those who fear a missing condition and will not cause confusion.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
